### Post by emarrodz7 on 2013-12-23
Hi everyone!

Some weeks ago I tried to install Ubuntu on a Pavilion DV4 but, as all partition were in use I wasn't able to do it. The recommendation I received was to shrink a partition and release some space for Ubuntu. Now I have a complete free partition but the now the installer only suggest to replace the Win7 OS instead to install along.

I tried to select the newly created partition but no luck. Any piece of advice? I'm feeling like a real noob so a step by step guide could be helpful ;) Remember, I want to keep the Win7 too.

Best regards!

---

### Post by Bucky Ball on 2013-12-23
Could you boot from a LiveDVD (the installer), get to a desktop, open Gparted and post a screenshot of it here so we can see what you have got there already.

If you have created an NTFS partition, delete it and just leave free space. If you have four partitions already, you are probably going to need to get rid of one of them and create an extended partition in its place.

During Ubuntu install you need to use 'Something Else' to manually partition. Are you selecting that option when you get to the partitioning section of the install?

---

### Post by fantab on 2013-12-24
> **Bucky Ball said:**
> Could you boot from a LiveDVD (the installer), get to a desktop, open Gparted and post a screenshot of it here so we can see what you have got there already.

While you are at it open Terminal [ctrl+alt+T], run the following commands and post its output here:

```
sudo parted -l
sudo fdisk -l
```

### Post by fantab on 2013-12-27
You formatted your last partitions, /dev/sda4 as 'NTFS'. You should NOT. Ubuntu/Linux will NOT install to NTFS partition.
Also you have MBR/'msdos' partition table, which means you have ONLY FOUR Primary Partition limit. Ubuntu will need a mimium of two partitions ('/' and 'swap').
So boot with Ubuntu DVD/USB, open Gparted, select the last partition, /dev/sda4 and DELETE it. From the Unallocated space create a 'new' EXTENDED PARTITION. Close Gparted and run the ubuntu installer and choose to install 'Alongside Windows' and it should install now.

If you want to take charge manually (recommended) the when installing ubuntu choose 'Something Else' at the Installation Type dialog:
After creating an Extended partition you will see that you still have 'unallocated space'. Select the 'unallocated space' and make a new partitions as LOGICAL. The following scheme should help:
20Gb LOGICAL [use as: ext4, mountpoint: /]
2-4Gb Logical [use as: linux_SWAP]
All the remaing Gb Logical [use as: ext4, mountpoint: /home]

Thats it. Continue and finish installation.

Good luck.

---

### Post by Bucky Ball on 2013-12-27
Also, do not resize Windows partition with Ubuntu/Linux. Use Win to do that. 

And yes, leave free space for you new install, not partitions, then choose 'Something Else' when you get to the partitioning section of the install. /, /home, /swap and others are there as default mount points, all pretty easy, but I do advise making a plan on how you want thing partitioned before commencing the install (although you have ample opportunity of changing things before confirming and hitting the big, red button of no return). ;)

---

### Post by oldfred on 2013-12-27
In addition to the 4 partition limit you created partitions with Windows and it does not use the standard extended partition, but converts to a proprietary dynamic partitioning scheme. Shown as SFS by fdisk.

       Microsofts offical policy is a full backup, erase dynamic partitions and create new basic partitions. There is no undo.
Dynamic volume is a Microsoft proprietary format developed together with Veritas (now acquired by Symantec) for logical volumes.
You may be use a third-party tool, such as Partition Wizard MiniTool or EASEUS to convert a convert a dynamic disk to a basic disk without having to delete or format them.
I've never used any of these and so I can't be sure they will work.Be sure to have good backups as any major partition change has risks.
Dynamic also on gpt as LDM
[http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/aa365449%28v=vs.85%29.aspx](http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/windows/desktop/aa365449%28v=vs.85%29.aspx)
[http://www.sevenforums.com/tutorials/26829-convert-dynamic-disk-basic-disk.html](http://www.sevenforums.com/tutorials/26829-convert-dynamic-disk-basic-disk.html)
From Linux view LDM
[http://mika.soup.io/post/304505086/ldmtool-accessing-Microsoft-Windows-dynamic-disks-from](http://mika.soup.io/post/304505086/ldmtool-accessing-Microsoft-Windows-dynamic-disks-from)

   Used EASEUS Partition Master -  free version used to  include conversion
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1692248](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1692248)
EASEUS Partition Master - The free home edition converted both dynamic partitions into basic partitions in less than 5 minutes!!
[http://www.partition-tool.com/personal.htm](http://www.partition-tool.com/personal.htm)

   Several users have used this, it has a liveCD download to use but you have to use the non-free version:
MiniTool Partition Wizard Professional Edition 5.2 to convert without loss of data the disk from dynamic disk to a basic disk.
also used Partition Wizard to set an existing partition logical instead of primary
Converted from dynamic with MiniTool, & repaired windows
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1779529](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1779529)
[http://www.partitionwizard.com/convertpartition/convert-to-basic-disk.html](http://www.partitionwizard.com/convertpartition/convert-to-basic-disk.html)
Partition wizard repaired NTFS partition table that gparted could not see with disk label error
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2112005](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2112005)

   EASEUS Partition Master 
[http://www.partition-tool.com/personal.htm](http://www.partition-tool.com/personal.htm)
Partition Wizard
[http://www.partitionwizard.com/free-partition-manager.html](http://www.partitionwizard.com/free-partition-manager.html)
 GRUB2 2.00 recognizes defunct LDM headers from old dynamic partitions
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/grub2/+bug/1061255](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/grub2/+bug/1061255)

### Post by oldfred on 2014-01-06
As long as you have the dynamic or SFS partition you will have issues with getting Linux to work. 

Also note that not all Windows tools work with dynamic partitions as they are not the standard basic partitions. They are logical partition overlay over the phyiscal partitions somewhat like LVM is in Linux.
